<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

	<div class="pure-g">
		<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.impactStatement || vm.details.abstract || vm.details.scope || vm.details.purpose  || vm.details.previewImage --><div ng-if="::vm.details.impactStatement || vm.details.abstract || vm.details.scope || vm.details.purpose  || vm.details.previewImage" ng-class="vm.details.graphicalAbstract ? 			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.impactStatement -->
		<!--/div-->
		<!--div ng-class="{'pure-u-14-24 u-pr-1':  vm.details.graphicalAbstract, 'pure-u-1-1': ! vm.details.graphicalAbstract}"-->
			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract --><div ng-if="::vm.details.abstract" class="ng-scope">
				<strong>Abstract:</strong>
				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">This paper presents a phase-noise reduction technique for voltage-controlled oscillators (VCOs) using a harmonic tuned (HT) LC tank. The phase-noise suppression is achieved through almost rectangular-shaped voltage at the switching differential cell, which effectively maximizes the slope of the switching cell output voltage at a zero crossing point. In addition, the proposed technique also suppresses the down-conversion of the noise around the second harmonic frequency by the second harmonic short of the tank. One second HT VCO and two third HT VCOs are designed and implemented to evaluate the concept using a 0.35- and 0.13-/spl mu/m CMOS process. The figure-of-merit (FOM) of the second HT VCO, third HT VCO1, and third HT VCO2 are -180.7, -183.7, and -189.5, respectively. The best FOM performance of the VCO has phase noises of -100.4, -132.0, and -140.8dBc/Hz at 100-kHz, 1-MHz, and 3-MHz offset frequencies at the 2-GHz carrier, respectively. This VCO consumes 3.29 mA from a 1.8-V supply with the silicon area of 500 /spl mu/m/spl times/750 /spl mu/m.</div>
			</div><!-- end ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract -->			
			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.scope -->
			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.purpose -->

<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>A major challenge in the wireless industry is the high-level integration of functional blocks using low-cost CMOS technology. Among the efforts for the single-chip radio integration, the implementation of a low phase-noise voltage-controlled oscillator (VCO) attracts a lot of attention because a phase noise of the VCO is one of the most critical parameters for the quality of service of the information transfer function. As CMOS downscaling is in progress for high level integration at a low cost, the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.685em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.505em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.5em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-3" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0031.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 10px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-4" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-5" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-6" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/002F.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 16px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-7" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0066.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 14px; vertical-align: -3px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.203em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">1/f</script></tex-math></inline-formula> corner frequency of the small-size transistors tends to increase and this is the crucial problem of the CMOS VCO. Moreover, the integration of a high-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-8" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.904em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.784em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.72em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-9" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-10" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0051.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; height: 15px; vertical-align: -3px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">Q</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <i>LC</i> tank is not easy due to the low resistivity of the silicon substrate, and this greatly affects the phase-noise performance. This paper presents an optimization technique for the phase-noise performance of the CMOS <i>LC</i> VCO, which reduces the flicker noise dominated <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-3-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-11" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 2.165em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.925em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.084em 1001.92em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-12" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-13" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.925em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1001.44em 4.447em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-14" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-15" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-16" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0031.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 10px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-17" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-18" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-19" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/002F.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0033.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 5px; height: 8px; vertical-align: 0px; width: 2.165em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.925em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.084em 1001.92em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-25" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-26" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; The phase-noise suppression is achieved through almost rectangular-shaped voltage at the switching differential cell, which effectively maximizes the slope of the switching cell output voltage at the zero crossing point. In addition, the proposed technique also suppresses down-conversion of the noise around <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-5-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-37" role="math" style="display: inline-block; height: 14px; vertical-align: -3px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; The optimized CMOS differential VCO delivers a measured phase noise, which is 10 dB lower than a conventional one in both <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-6-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-47" role="math" style="display: inline-block; <div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Phase-Noise Issues and VCO Design</h2></div><div class="section_2" id="sec2a"><h3>A. Phase-Noise Minimization</h3><p>Recently, the theory and analysis for the physical processes of the phase noise in differential oscillators have made significant progress, and the techniques to lower the phase noise have advanced through the understanding of these phase-noise mechanisms <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_2a">[1]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_2a">[2]</a>. The phase noise is mainly induced from various mixing phenomena of the negative <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-8-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-73" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.204em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1001.08em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-74" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-75" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.48em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-76" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-77" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-78" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0067.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 10px; vertical-align: -3px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.781em; left: 0.423em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-79" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-80" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-81" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/238/006D.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 5px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-8">{g}_{m}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> switching differential pair. One of the main mixing phenomena is up- and down-conversion from the thermal noise component at the baseband and the harmonics of the oscillation frequency. The other one is up-conversion from the flicker noise in baseband to the phase noise in the fundamental frequency. The well-known phase-noise model for an oscillator is Leeson's proportionality <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_2a">[3]</a> <disp-formula id="deqn1" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><div class="MathJax_Display"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-9-Frame" tabindex="0" style="width: 100%;"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-82" role="math" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0061.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 6px; height: 5px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-262" style="display: inline-block; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.803em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-16">g_{m{\rm bias}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the transconductance of the currentâsource FET <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_2a">[4]</a>. The first and second terms in <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn2" href="#deqn2" class="fulltext-link">(2)</a> describe the phase-noise contributions from the resonator loss and differential-pair FETs, respectively. The third term in <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn2" href="#deqn2" class="fulltext-link">(2)</a> signifies the phase noise produced by down-conversion of the CS noise component at the second harmonic of the oscillation frequency. The second term can be reduced by increasing <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-17-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-263" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.084em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.96em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-264" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-265" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-266" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-267" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-268" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0056.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; height: 12px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: -0.177em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.183em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.544em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-269" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-270" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-271" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/238/006F.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 5px; height: 5px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.003em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-17">{V}_{o}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, which is the voltage across the resonator and is proportional to the slope at the zero crossing voltage of the switching cell <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_2a">[4]</a>. Thus, increasing <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-18-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-272" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.084em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.96em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-273" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-274" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-275" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-276" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-277" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0056.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; height: 12px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: -0.177em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.183em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.544em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-278" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-279" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-280" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/238/006F.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 5px; height: 5px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.003em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-18">{V}_{o}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> means a steep rise at the zero crossing point. To realize the concept, we have employed a harmonic tuned (HT) <i>LC</i> tank, which can deliver a square waveform voltage to the cell <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_2a">[5]</a>. From this concept, we have fabricated three VCOs and compared them with the standard VCOs.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec2b"><h3>B. Third HT <i>LC</i> Tank Design</h3><p>The proposed <i>LC</i> tank is tuned up to the third harmonics, open at the fundamental frequency and third harmonic, and short at the second harmonic, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>. The center tank resonates at the fundamental frequency and the two side tanks resonate at the third harmonic, while the combined one provides the second harmonic short. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2</a> shows the schematic of the differential <i>LC</i> VCO with the tanks. The simulated output waveforms of the oscillator at the output node A and B of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2</a> are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a>. This waveform indicates the reduced noise from the switching core. The HT <i>LC</i> tank presents shortness at the second harmonic and stabilizes the tail voltage fluctuation, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a>. Thus, through harmonic tuning, we can reduce the phase noise induced by the CS. Actually, since the phase noise from the resonator loss is also induced via modulation of zero crossing instants of the differential pair, harmonic tuning can also reduce the resonator noise portion.

border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.088em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-20">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> terminations.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/1650429/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>

The noise sources for the up-conversion are the tail current source (CS) and negative <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-22-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-299" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.204em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1001.08em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-300" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-301" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.48em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-302" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-303" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-304" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0067.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 10px; vertical-align: -3px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.781em; left: 0.423em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-305" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-306" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-307" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/238/006D.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 5px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-22">{g}_{m}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> switching differential pair. The flicker noise from the tail CS is converted to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-23-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-308" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.964em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.844em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.84em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-309" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-310" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.844em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.54em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-311" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-312" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-313" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0066.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 14px; vertical-align: -3px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.781em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-314" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-315" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-316" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0030.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 5px; height: 8px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-23">{f}_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> due to the mixing action of the VCO circuit and the noise is delivered to the resonator as an AM noise <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_2b">[6]</a>. After that, the AM noise is converted into an FM noise by the tuning varactor <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_2b">[1]</a>. The FM sidebands appear as the close-in phase noise. The AM to FM conversion depends on the gain of the varactor and can be minimized by reducing the size of the CMOS varactor, while a wide tuning can be implemented by a capacitor array, which is switched on and off in parallel with the <i>LC</i> tank <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_2b">[2]</a>. The switched tuning method is not adopted in this paper for a simple structure. Instead, a pMOS CS with a large gate length of 3 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-24-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-317" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.505em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1001.32em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-318" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-319" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/03BC.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 11px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-320" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-321" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-322" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-323" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-324" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/006D.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 13px; height: 7px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.803em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-24">\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is used for less <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-25-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-325" role="math" style="display: inline-block; height: 10px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-328" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-329" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-330" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/002F.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 16px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-331" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0066.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 14px; vertical-align: -3px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; </p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/34611/1650429/1650429-fig-5-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/34611/1650429/1650429-fig-5-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 5. </b><fig><p>Simulated result of the magnitude of the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-26-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-332" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.863em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.665em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.26em 1000.66em 2.384em -999.997em); top: -2.179em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-333" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-334" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0053.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 10px; height: 12px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: -0.063em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.069em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.186em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.088em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-26">S</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameter of: (a) main and second harmonic tuning <i>LC</i> tanks and (b) total second HT <i>LC</i> tank.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/1650429/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
Additionally, the tail node (the common mode node of the CS) oscillates at twice of the oscillation frequency <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-27-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-335" role="math" style="display: inline-block; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-341" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0066.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 14px; vertical-align: -3px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.781em; left: 0.964em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-342" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-343" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-344" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0030.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 5px; height: 8px; vertical-align: 0px; As a result, the flicker noise of the CS is up-converted to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-28-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-345" role="math" style="display: inline-block; top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-346" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-347" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0032.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-348" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.844em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; height: 14px; vertical-align: -3px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-350" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-351" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-352" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0030.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 5px; height: 8px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-28">2f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> through channel length modulation and it is mixed down to the oscillation frequency again and presents the close-in phase noise <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_2b">[6]</a>. Therefore, to minimize the up-conversion of flicker noise from the tail CS, all even harmonics must be suppressed. The suppression of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-29-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-353" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.505em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.32em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-354" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-355" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0032.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 11px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-356" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.844em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.54em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-357" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0066.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 14px; vertical-align: -3px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-358" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-359" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-360" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/238/0030.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 5px; height: 8px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-29">2f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> made by the second harmonic short circuit at the tail node (the common-mode node of the CS) can minimize the phase noise from the CS. The flicker noise from the switching differential pair modulates the second harmonic voltage waveform at the common source node in every half period, which induces a noisy current in the parasitic capacitance at the source of each switching pair. This current is mixed down to the fundamental frequency by the switching pair, inducing the close-in phase noise. This phase noise is actually a small portion due to the switching nature of the oscillator, but this portion can be increased with downscaling of CMOS to nanosize. Though the CS flicker noise can be minimized by using MOS transistors with relatively large gate length, the nanosize transistors should be used for the switching pair for high-frequency operation and can be a problem in the nano-CMOS process. The <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-30-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-361" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.685em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.505em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.5em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-362" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-363" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0031.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 10px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-364" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-365" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-366" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/002F.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 16px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-367" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0066.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 14px; vertical-align: -3px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.203em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-30">1/f</script></tex-math></inline-formula> noise in MOSFET is mainly caused by the carrier (de)trapping in localized oxide states. The switching with 50% duty cycle removes all memory in a silicon oxide state and it can be a means to reduce the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-31-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-368" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.685em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.505em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.5em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-369" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-370" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0031.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 10px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-371" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-372" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-373" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/002F.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 16px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-374" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0066.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 14px; vertical-align: -3px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.203em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-31">1/f</script></tex-math></inline-formula> noise itself by forcing the trap to release its captured electron <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_2b">[7]</a>. The proposed harmonic tuning makes the oscillating wave rectangular, much like an ideal switching with 50% duty cycle. As a result, it can reduce the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-32-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-375" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.685em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.505em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.5em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-376" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-377" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/0031.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 10px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-378" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-379" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-380" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/002F.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 7px; height: 16px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-381" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0066.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 14px; vertical-align: -3px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.203em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-32">1/f</script></tex-math></inline-formula> noise at the switching core.<p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec2c"><h3>C. Second HT <i>LC</i> Tank Design</h3><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/34611/1650429/1650429-fig-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/34611/1650429/1650429-fig-6-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 6. </b><fig><p>VCO with the second HT <i>LC</i> tank.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/1650429/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/34611/1650429/1650429-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/34611/1650429/1650429-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 7. </b><fig><p>Simulated output voltage waveform for: (a) standard <i>LC</i> VCO and (b) second HT <i>LC</i> VCO.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/1650429/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
The third HT <i>LC</i> tank can reduce the phase noise significantly by maximizing the slope of the output voltage wave at the zero crossing point and by suppressing the second harmonic at the tail node. However, it needs two inductors, which increase the chip area. To compromise the tradeoff between the slope at the zero crossing point and chip size, we have tried the second HT <i>LC</i> tank. Similar to the third HT tank, the second HT <i>LC</i> tank is open at the fundamental frequency and short at the second harmonic, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a>. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a> shows the proposed VCO with the second HT <i>LC</i> tank. It reduces the second harmonic power at the drain of the CS. The VCO also increases the slope of the output voltage wave at the zero crossing point, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a>. <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a> shows the simulated phase-noise contribution for the standard and second tuned <i>LC</i> VCOs at 100-kHz offset from the center frequency. The proposed second harmonic tuning technique can suppress the phase noise from various noise sources including the negative <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-33-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-382" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.204em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1001.08em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-383" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-384" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.48em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-385" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-386" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-387" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0067.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 10px; vertical-align: -3px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.781em; left: 0.423em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-388" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-389" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-390" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/238/006D.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 5px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-33">{g}_{m}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> core transistors. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a> shows the simulated phase noises of VCO1, VCO2, and VCO3 at 1-GHz carrier frequency as a function of the offset frequency and at offset frequencies of 100 kHz and 3 MHz as a function of carrier frequency. VCO1 is a standard <i>LC</i> VCO, VCO2 is the second HT <i>LC</i> VCO, and VCO3 is a standard VCO, which has bigger capacitor to fit the oscillation frequency to VCO2. Since the VCO2 has larger parasitic capacitance than VCO1 due to some additional component, the VCO1 has slightly higher carrier frequencies than VCO2. To compare phase noises between VCOs with the same carrier frequency, the phase noise of VCO3 is added in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a>. The phase-noise improvement of the second HT <i>LC</i> VCO is 3â6 dB in all oscillation frequencies.
<div class="figure figure-full table" id="table1"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table I </b>Phase-Noise Contribution of the Second HT LC VCO<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/34611/1650429/1650429-table-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/34611/1650429/1650429-table-1-small.gif" alt="Table I" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/34611/1650429/1650429-fig-8-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/34611/1650429/1650429-fig-8-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 8. </b><fig><p>Simulated phase noise of the three VCOs: (a) at 1-GHz carrier frequency and at (b) 100-kHz and (c) 3-MHz offset frequencies.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/1650429/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec2d"><h3>D. Third HT <i>LC</i> Tank With Noise Filtering Technique</h3><p>The harmonic tuning technique reduces the switching time, from the on to the off state, of the negative <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-34-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-391" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.204em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1001.08em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-392" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-393" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.48em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-394" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-395" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-396" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0067.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 10px; vertical-align: -3px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.781em; left: 0.423em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-397" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-398" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-399" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/238/006D.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 5px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-34">{g}_{m}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> cell by increasing the slope of the output voltage wave at the zero crossing point. However, it cannot reduce the phase noise from the device itself. To reduce the phase noise effectively, the noise filtering technique is commonly adopted <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_2d">[2]</a>. In a standard top-biased VCO, the common-source node of the N-MOS switching pair is connected to the ground. It forces one of the N-MOSs into the triode region as the rising differential oscillation voltage crosses <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-35-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-400" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.204em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.08em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-401" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-402" style="display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-403" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-404" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-405" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0056.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; height: 12px; vertical-align: -1px; margin-right: -0.177em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.183em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.544em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-406" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-407" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-408" style="display: inline-block; font-size: 70.7%;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/238/0054.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 8px; height: 8px; margin-right: -0.117em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; Thus, the average resonator <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-36-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-409" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 0.904em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.784em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.72em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-410" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-411" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0051.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; height: 15px; vertical-align: -3px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-36">Q</script></tex-math></inline-formula> factor over a full oscillation cycle is reduced, degrading the overall phase noise. The filtering, by parallel resonation at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-37-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-412" role="math" style="display: inline-block; Using these techniques, a complementary VCO is designed to achieve the minimum phase noise. The phase-noise simulation results in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 10</a> show the phase-noise reduction effect of each technique independently and also that of the combined case. The phase-noise contributions of the various noise components of the test VCO at 100-kHz offset frequency are summarized in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table2" class="fulltext-link">Table II</a>. <div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Measurement Results</h2></div><p>In this study, three types of VCOs are designed, implemented, and measured. The first one is the VCO with the second HT <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-46-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-487" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.565em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.38em 2.345em -999.997em); height: 11px; margin-right: 0.063em;" /></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-490" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/0043.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 12px; height: 12px; vertical-align: 0px; margin-right: -0.057em;" /><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-47">LC</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and noise filtering technique <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_3">[8]</a>, and the last one <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_3">[9]</a> is the same architecture of the second one, but it is designed with another process to check the dependency for another process and frequency. The first is called the âsecond HT VCOâ, the second one is called the âthird HT VCO1â, and the last one is called the âthird HT VCO2.â</p><p>The âsecond HT VCOâ and âthird HT VCO1â are fabricated in a 0.35-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-48-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-495" role="math" style="display: inline-block; height: 11px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-498" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-499" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-500" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-501" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-502" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/006D.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 13px; height: 7px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.803em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-48">\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> CMOS process of STMicroelectronics, Paris, France. The âthird HT VCO2â is fabricated in a 0.13-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-49-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-503" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.505em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1001.32em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-504" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-505" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Math/Italic/336/03BC.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 9px; height: 11px; vertical-align: -4px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-506" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-507" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-508" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-509" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-510" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/006D.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 13px; height: 7px; margin-right: 0.003em;" /></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.803em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-49">\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> CMOS process of the Samsung Electronic Company Ltd., Yongin, Gyeunggi, Korea. The chips are measured on an HP4352S VCO/phase locked-loop (PLL) signal test system.</p><div class="section_2" id="sec3a"><h3>A. Second HT VCO</h3><p>The microphotograph of the fabricated chip with a 0.6 mm <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-50-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-511" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.024em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.505em 1000.9em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-512" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-513" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/00D7.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 10px; height: 8px; margin-right: 0.123em;" /></span><span class="mspace" id="MathJax-Span-514" style="display: inline-block; height: 0.003em; vertical-align: 0.003em; width: 0.183em; overflow: hidden;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-50">\times\,</script></tex-math></inline-formula>0.65 mm area is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 11</a>. The frequency of oscillation could be tuned from 900 MHz to 1.05 GHz, which yields a tuning range of approximately 15%. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 12(a)</a> shows the phase noise versus the offset frequency for the standard VCO and second HT VCO at 1 GHz. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 12(b)</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">(c)</a> shows the phase noise of the two VCOs as a function of the carrier frequency, measured at offset frequencies of 100 kHz and 3 MHz, respectively. The phase-noise reduction by the second harmonic tuning is from 4 to 7 dB. These measurement results show a good agreement with the simulation results, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a>.

Third HT VCO1</h3><p>The microphotograph of the fabricated chip with 1.2 mm <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-51-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-515" role="math" style="display: inline-block; width: 1.024em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.505em 1000.9em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-516" style="display: inline-block;"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-517" style="display: inline-block;"><img src="http://staticieeexplore.ieee.org/xploreAssets/MathJax-2.6.1/fonts/HTML-CSS/TeX/png/Main/Regular/336/00D7.png?rev=2.6.1" style="width: 10px; height: 8px; margin-right: 0.123em;" /></span><span class="mspace" id="MathJax-Span-518" style="display: inline-block; height: 0.003em; vertical-align: 0.003em; width: 0.183em; overflow: hidden;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-51">\times\,</script></tex-math></inline-formula>0.43 mm area is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig13" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 13</a>. width: 1.024em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.505em 1000.9em 2.345em -999.997em); Since the area of the optimized VCO is not effectively utilized for these test chips due to the location of the RF PADs, the increment of the area is relative large for the third HT VCO1. The VCO is tunable from 1.89 to 2.17 GHz. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig16" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 16</a> shows the phase noise versus the offset frequencies for the standard VCO and third HT VCO2. The phase-noise reduction due to the third harmonic tuning and the noise filtering techniques is over 10 dB at the same frequency shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig17" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 17</a>. </p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table4"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table IV </b>VCO Performance Comparison<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/34611/1650429/1650429-table-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/34611/1650429/1650429-table-4-small.gif" alt="Table IV" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div><p></p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Conclusions</h2></div><p>We have presented a technique to lower the phase noise of <i>LC</i> oscillators using the HT <i>LC</i> tank. The phase-noise suppression is achieved through almost rectangular-shaped voltage at the switching differential cell, which effectively maximizes the slope of the switching cell output voltage at zero crossing point. Beside the sharp switching, the proposed technique suppresses the down-conversion of the noise around the second harmonic frequency by the second harmonic short of the tank. It also reduces the differential pair flicker noise itself and is useful to down-scaling of CMOS technology. Three VCOs are implemented and measured to check the concept. To compromise the tradeoff between the slope at a zero crossing point and chip size, we have tried the second HT <i>LC</i> tank. The second HT <i>LC</i> VCO has less phase-noise improvement than the third HT <i>LC</i> VCO, but is smaller than the third one. The improvement of the proposed technique appears over a broad control voltage range. <script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

		}
	}
});

The phase-noise suppression is achieved through almost rectangular-shaped voltage at the switching differential cell, which effectively maximizes the slope of the switching cell output voltage at a zero crossing point. In addition, the proposed technique also suppresses the down-conversion of the noise around the second harmonic frequency by the second harmonic short of the tank. One second HT VCO and two third HT VCOs are designed and implemented to evaluate the concept using a 0.35- and 0.13-/spl mu/m CMOS process. The figure-of-merit (FOM) of the second HT VCO, third HT VCO1, and third HT VCO2 are -180.7, -183.7, and -189.5, respectively. The best FOM performance of the VCO has phase noises of -100.4, -132.0, and -140.8dBc/Hz at 100-kHz, 1-MHz, and 3-MHz offset frequencies at the 2-GHz carrier, respectively. This VCO consumes 3.29 mA from a 1.8-V supply with the silicon area of 500 /spl mu/m/spl times/750 /spl
